    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5789353-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605042512p2/5789353.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/289482636?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/5789353-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=bought-in-store">bought-in-store</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=arc-physical">arc-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=genre-action-adventure">genre-action-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=unsolicited">unsolicited</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=from-publishers">from-publishers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=genre-dystopia">genre-dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=age-young-adult">age-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=genre-survival">genre-survival</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer289482636" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4262327318434899333">A finished unsolicited copy was provided by the publisher for review.<br/><br/>Global warming has devastated the entire planet, and oxygen levels are at an all time low. The survivors have found a way to live in domed cities which are erected around the planet by the corporation Breathe. They control the oxygen consumption of everyone in the city. Lower class citizens must pay for their oxygen, while wealthier classes have an unlimited supply. Quinn, the handsome, wealthy Premium whose father works for th</span>
  <span id="freeText4262327318434899333" style="display:none">A finished unsolicited copy was provided by the publisher for review.<br /><br />Global warming has devastated the entire planet, and oxygen levels are at an all time low. The survivors have found a way to live in domed cities which are erected around the planet by the corporation Breathe. They control the oxygen consumption of everyone in the city. Lower class citizens must pay for their oxygen, while wealthier classes have an unlimited supply. Quinn, the handsome, wealthy Premium whose father works for the Breathe corporation. Bea, who is an auxiliary, and also Quinn's best friend happens to be in love with him (Can we say love triangle?). Alina, the headstrong gorgeous girl who happens to be part of the Resistance. Can they all work together to save the dome and everyone who lives in it from further destruction?<br /><br />Breathe is broken up into multiple viewpoints of the three characters Bea, Quinn and Alina. I always liked how authors do this just because you can see what the other character is thinking about the author. I especially enjoy reading about the viewpoint of the boy. Sometimes their viewpoints make me laugh. In this case, Quinn's viewpoint made me roar with laughter. Some of his thoughts are quite hilarious. I didn't care very much about Alina though. She was a tad snobby, and only cared about herself. Bea on the other hand is the sweetheart, and had a lot of sympathy for Maude.<br /><br />There wasn't a whole lot of character development through out the novel, so if you're looking for fully developed characters in this novel, then it isn't for you. Although, if you want a fast paced and exciting read, then Breathe is definitely what you're looking for. I don't think I will ever tire of dystopian themed novels, and Breathe was no exception. Survival, freedom, chaos, and rebellion all rolled into one. I loved the plot! The story kept me turning the pages, and I read this one in one sitting. I'm glad the romance wasn't the focus (thank God!). I can't wait to see what else Sarah Crossan has in store for us.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4262327318434899333" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_352987316" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/352987316" />
    <a title="Jon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4277731-jon"><img alt="Jon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1384212540p2/4277731.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/352987316?book_show_action=true">Jun 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jon" href="/user/show/4277731-jon">Jon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4277731-jon?shelf=dystopia-post-apocalyptic">dystopia-post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4277731-jon?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer352987316" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2866683042621701888"> <a href='http://scottreadsit.blogspot.com/2012/10/breathe-by-sarah-crossan.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Find this review at Scott Reads It</a><br/><br/> **Thank you to Greenwillow Books for providing me with an ARC in exchange for an honest review**<br/><br/> Breathe had a lot of promise in my opinion but it really disappointed me. Imagine a world where people live inside a dome and outside is pretty much ruins (Under The Never Sky) then imagine that inside the dome people need oxygen masks to survive (Masque of the Red Death). Breathe takes in place in a dome ruled by a government called Breathe.<br/> <br/> This book is told fro</span>
  <span id="freeText2866683042621701888" style="display:none"> <a href="http://scottreadsit.blogspot.com/2012/10/breathe-by-sarah-crossan.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Find this review at Scott Reads It</a><br /><br /> **Thank you to Greenwillow Books for providing me with an ARC in exchange for an honest review**<br /><br /> Breathe had a lot of promise in my opinion but it really disappointed me. Imagine a world where people live inside a dome and outside is pretty much ruins (Under The Never Sky) then imagine that inside the dome people need oxygen masks to survive (Masque of the Red Death). Breathe takes in place in a dome ruled by a government called Breathe.<br /> <br /> This book is told from the POV of three different characters (1 male, and 2 females). The POV was a bit of a problem for me because Alina and Bea sounded pretty similar and I had to flip back to see who was talking. I like books where the characters have distinct voices but this wasn't the case with Breathe.<br /><br />All the characters in Breathe weren't too likeable in my opinion. Be warned there is a cliche and typical love triangle! Quinn is in love with Alina even though he doesn't really know her. Alina doesn't really love anybody and Bea is obsessed with Quinn. Why is Quinn too blind to see that Bea has liked him since they were little? I'll tell you why! It's a stereotypical generic love triangle that we have seen so often in media. The male best friend always falls in love with someone new and foreign to him. He never opens his eyes and sees that his best friend loves him more than a friend.<br /><br /> I am not a big fan of Breathe but it was a decent read. It had action and adventure along with romance. It was in my opinion, a typical dystopia even though the plot sounded original. Breathe in my opinion was pretty cliche and was very predictable!! I don't recommend this book at all but I'm clearly the minority here. I definitely won't be reading the sequel to Breathe. If you're in the mood for a great dystopian read Under The Never Sky instead!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2866683042621701888" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_396318208" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/396318208" />

  <div class="left bodycol">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13634032-breathe">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3835702-kat?shelf=arc-review-complete">arc-review-complete</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3835702-kat?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3835702-kat?shelf=udate">udate</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3835702-kat?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer396318208" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17838680125812588702">If I saw Breathe displayed in a bookshop, I'd pick it up. If I read the synopsis, I'd trot right over the cashier, hand over my hard-earned cash, go home and start reading straight away. It looks good, it sounds good, so it MUST be good.<br/><br/>However, I struggled to enjoy Breathe. I'm not adverse to multiple POV stories, however the flashes between Alina, Quinn and Bea were so fast that I struggled to keep up with exactly who was narrating and when, although it was also essential to the story to show </span>
  <span id="freeText17838680125812588702" style="display:none">If I saw Breathe displayed in a bookshop, I'd pick it up. If I read the synopsis, I'd trot right over the cashier, hand over my hard-earned cash, go home and start reading straight away. It looks good, it sounds good, so it MUST be good.<br /><br />However, I struggled to enjoy Breathe. I'm not adverse to multiple POV stories, however the flashes between Alina, Quinn and Bea were so fast that I struggled to keep up with exactly who was narrating and when, although it was also essential to the story to show all their experiences. Yep I realise I'm being completely contradictory.<br /><br />The characters are probably the part I struggled with the most, overall. Alina isn't a likeable character - and when she does a pretty radical 180 and suddenly cares deeply about everyone I couldn't work out why, or when, this miraculous change of heart actually happened. <br /> <br />Quinn is a sterotypical stupid rich boy who is best friends with a smart, caring girl but doesn't realise it, and instead crushes on a girl that doesn't seem to have any redeamable features.<br /><br />Bea was pretty much the only main character that I actually liked because although her family was not as rich or influential as Quinn's, she's clever and kind.<br /><br />Breathe is a believable world as a possible scenario of what could happen if we continue to treat the planet like a big dumping ground, and the idea of a world with no trees, no flowers and living on synthetic foodstuffs is pretty disturbing. The science is well explained, and the world of the dome, and the outlands is very well built, with far more showing than telling.<br /><br />And although all the ingredients for a tension-filled, action-packed book are there, I had trouble buying into the whole menacing vibe - it felt more like the trio were a bunch of naughty schoolkids that would be grounded, not that their lives were in danger.<br /><br />Overall for me, Breathe is a book that had so much potential and some good features, but the lack of care I had for the characters, the fact that I could have lazily read the whole 400 pages in 4 hours and the confusingly fast POV switches just left me underwhelmed.<br /><br />Read more of my reviews at <a href="http://theaussiezombie.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">The Aussie Zombie</a></span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10426319351935414834">The concept of this was good. The world doesn't have anymore trees, therefore they don't have oxygen. Everywhere around them looks dead, like there isn't any life to it. To live they have these air tanks that they carry around with them but they are limited to activity. The poor people can barely make it and they don't really have a lot of food for their family. They don't have much money to spend on their oxygen. That's how they have everything sent up. The premiums, which are kind of like the </span>
  <span id="freeText10426319351935414834" style="display:none">The concept of this was good. The world doesn't have anymore trees, therefore they don't have oxygen. Everywhere around them looks dead, like there isn't any life to it. To live they have these air tanks that they carry around with them but they are limited to activity. The poor people can barely make it and they don't really have a lot of food for their family. They don't have much money to spend on their oxygen. That's how they have everything sent up. The premiums, which are kind of like the rich, they can afford to get more oxygen and better food. They are treated better. The place that is in charge is called Breathe, but are they really telling the truth about everything? Are all the trees really completely gone? What about the plants? Anyways, that is what you find out in reading this book. It had me hooked in the beginning. It's about 3.5 stars to me in my opinion.</span>

<div id="review_352765677" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/352765677" />
    <a title="Lisbeth Avery {Domus Libri}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8282085-lisbeth-avery-domus-libri"><img alt="Lisbeth Avery {Domus Libri}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1426613564p2/8282085.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/352765677?book_show_action=true">Jun 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisbeth Avery {Domus Libri}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisbeth Avery {Domus Libri}" href="/user/show/8282085-lisbeth-avery-domus-libri">Lisbeth Avery {Domus Libri}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8282085-lisbeth-avery-domus-libri?shelf=abandoned">abandoned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8282085-lisbeth-avery-domus-libri?shelf=could-have-been-better">could-have-been-better</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8282085-lisbeth-avery-domus-libri?shelf=no-star">no-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer352765677" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17966416976536100964"><i>I didn’t finish this book.<br/>I didn’t get past 80%.<br/>I will review it though.<br/><br/>If you don’t want to read a DNF review. Click the back button. Close the browser. I don’t care. If you do want to read this, continue down the review.</i><br/><br/>——<br/><br/>I didn’t like Breathe. When you read DNF, you probably assumed I hated it. I did not hate it. I simply got bored with it. I didn’t care about what happened to the characters or the fictional world. Truthfully, I lost track of the story at 55 – 60% in. I really hate when that </span>
  <span id="freeText17966416976536100964" style="display:none"><i>I didn’t finish this book.<br />I didn’t get past 80%.<br />I will review it though.<br /><br />If you don’t want to read a DNF review. Click the back button. Close the browser. I don’t care. If you do want to read this, continue down the review.</i><br /><br />——<br /><br />I didn’t like Breathe. When you read DNF, you probably assumed I hated it. I did not hate it. I simply got bored with it. I didn’t care about what happened to the characters or the fictional world. Truthfully, I lost track of the story at 55 – 60% in. I really hate when that happens. When it gets to the point when you have no idea what happened, why continue?<br /><br /><b>Characters:</b><br />The book switches between three POVS: Bea’s, Quinn’s, and Alina’s.<br /><br />Bea is in love with Quinn. Like swoon, fall over in love. She was annoying and pretty bland. She was the average heroine of the story. Quinn is in lust with Alina. He doesn’t even realize his friend has green eyes. He is pretty boring to read about. Alina couldn’t care less about Bea or Quinn. She is the bad girl of the story. She was pretty mediocre for the bad girl.<br /><br />They weren’t bad characters. I just found them boring and unrelatable<br /><br /><b>Plot &amp; Writing:</b><br /><i>Plot:</i><br />Wow, the idea was amazing. A world with no air? This could go far.<br /><br />But instead, there was an unnecessary, undeveloped rebellion and some sort of nature walk. I don’t really get why they’re walking out and why they are still following Alina, even though they know something’s up with her. The plot didn’t really make any sense and as a result I couldn’t follow it.<br /><br /><i>Writing:</i><br />The writing had a lot of problems. There were weird things in the ARC that didn’t make any sense (such as a guy talking with no air) but other wise it was pretty standard. The writing lacked a lot of emotion.<br /><br /><b>What I liked and didn’t:</b><br />Liked:<br />• The Multiple POVS<br />• The interesting idea<br />• Interesting beginning<br /><br />Disliked:<br />• Lack of originality<br />• Not really doing anything with lack of air. More of a side problem than anything else<br />• Story tapers off at 50%<br />• boring characters<br /><br /><b>In conclusion:</b><br />Breathe is not for everyone. I didn’t like it, but you might, though!<br /><br />————————————————————————<br /><br /><b>Favorite Character:</b> N/A<br /><b>Favorite Quote:</b> <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>N/A</i>

<div id="review_421845700" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/421845700" />
    <a title="Sandra " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9752625-sandra"><img alt="Sandra " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1345749155p2/9752625.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/421845700?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandra " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandra " href="/user/show/9752625-sandra">Sandra </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9752625-sandra?shelf=reviewed-books">reviewed-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9752625-sandra?shelf=horrible-bad-boring-beginnings">horrible-bad-boring-beginnings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9752625-sandra?shelf=cliffhangers">cliffhangers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer421845700" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3550018385407364012">In a world with no trees, no air, no truth... There is no choice but to fight back.<br/><br/>Breathe by Sara Crossan is a dystopia describing life in a new society that has arisen following the collapse of the one that we know. And it's the first in a trilogy, thus the story is a long way from being resolved by the end of this volume. It runs for three hundred and seventy one pages. And is divided into five parts [four long and one very short] and fifty seven chapters.<br/><br/>So far so familiar.<br/><br/>So what does Breat</span>
  <span id="freeText3550018385407364012" style="display:none">In a world with no trees, no air, no truth... There is no choice but to fight back.<br /><br />Breathe by Sara Crossan is a dystopia describing life in a new society that has arisen following the collapse of the one that we know. And it's the first in a trilogy, thus the story is a long way from being resolved by the end of this volume. It runs for three hundred and seventy one pages. And is divided into five parts [four long and one very short] and fifty seven chapters.<br /><br />So far so familiar.<br /><br />So what does Breathe offer to make it stand out in a rather crowded genre and marketplace?<br /><br />It's the story of life in the world after the Switch. In a treeless world, oxygen levels have plunged. And only a few get to live in the Pod. A self contained habitation, divided into various zones. Air is provided by the breathe corporation. Who give the residents regular vaccinations. Society is divided into two groups. Premiums and auxiliaries. Only the former are able to afford to live a good life.<br />Anyone who doesn't go along with society in the Pod is ejected. And anyone living outside the Pod may not last long, as there's not a lot of air there.<br /><br />There are 3 main characters. 1)Bea. 2)Quinn. 3)Alina. They each have a very different personality's. <br /><br />The beginning was pure TORTURE for me. I couldn't get into it. I hated the characters and the book itself. But after like 150 pages it got better and better. It got so good in fact, that i couldn't put it down. I started to like the characters and the plot. <br /><br />Speaking of characters. There IS a love triangle. But it was just till the middle of the book ( which is good, cause i'm getting tired of those love triangles). It was like this - Bea was secretly in love with her best friend Quinn, but Quinn had a crush on Alina ( a girl he have just met), and Alina had a crush on this boy called Abel ( who died pretty soon). It then, thank god, get's sorted out. Quinn finally sees Bea and how beautiful she is and u know whats gonna happen, ' love is in the air' yada yada. It was really bugging me, this love triangle, I'm ok with having the ' 2 boys fighting over a girl' type of triangle, but the other way around triangles? Not so much.<br /><br />I don't know what else to say.<br /><br />Just to reassure any non-romantic potential readers that despite the love triangle it really isn't a lovely touchy feel book but actually a really good and at most times action packed book. I really enjoyed this book and shall definitely be on the look out for the next in the series.<br /><br />Breathe is very enjoyable but I do think there are better dystopian YA novels out there. I will pick up the next book in the series because I believe there is potential here.<br /><br />Overall, Breathe is an amazing book! Leaves you on a cliff hanger, I actually shouted "more!". Definitely worth a read, you will not be left disappointed. Just wish I didn't have to wait a year for the next one.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3550018385407364012" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Annabelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1235083-annabelle"><img alt="Annabelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1348368292p2/1235083.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1235083-annabelle?shelf=cliffhangers">cliffhangers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1235083-annabelle?shelf=gorgeous-cover">gorgeous-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1235083-annabelle?shelf=books-that-made-me-cry">books-that-made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1235083-annabelle?shelf=best-books-in-the-world">best-books-in-the-world</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer331088490" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3337771429676142668">*****FINAL RATING: 4.80 STARS*****<br/><br/><b>
  <u>CATCHALL</u>
</b><br/>I absolutely adored this book. It is seriously one of my favorite reads of 2012. It is without a doubt completely unlike anything I've ever read. Not your formulaic dystopian, Breathe has some serious action balanced by some killer romance! The characters were incredibly likable and the plot and the writing made me absolutely fall in love. Everything about it was original and fresh, and I loved some of the brilliant ideas involved. One of my favorite</span>
  <span id="freeText3337771429676142668" style="display:none">*****FINAL RATING: 4.80 STARS*****<br /><br /><b>
  <u>CATCHALL</u>
</b><br />I absolutely adored this book. It is seriously one of my favorite reads of 2012. It is without a doubt completely unlike anything I've ever read. Not your formulaic dystopian, Breathe has some serious action balanced by some killer romance! The characters were incredibly likable and the plot and the writing made me absolutely fall in love. Everything about it was original and fresh, and I loved some of the brilliant ideas involved. One of my favorite ever books for sure, Breathe has found a place in my heart.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE HEROINES</u>
</b><br /><u>ALINE</u><br />Aline is a really hard and sometimes insensitive character, but she never backs down from what she believes in. She lets her guard down one and that's enough to scare her into becoming someone she's not. Bold and brave, Aline seems like she's not afraid of anything, but inside she can be conflicted. She's one of the most human characters I've ever read about and while in the beginning it was a struggle to identify with her, I quickly found myself pulled into her character.<br /><u>BEA</u><br />Bea is as amazing a heroine as Aline, but in a completely different way. She's quiet but brilliant. She's spent her whole life following the rules, doing what she's told—until she meets Aline and begins to question everything she was taught. Instead of shrinking back, she finally learns to stand up for herself and she does what's right. Bea is an extremely relatable character, and definitely has a bit of every girl in her.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE HERO</u>
</b><br /><u>QUINN</u><br />Despite his name, which you will never convince me is not a girl name, Quinn is actually a pretty awesome character. He's adorably dense and constantly misses what's right in front of him. Sure, that's a tad cliché, but whatever! Quinn, unlike Aline and Bea, is from the privileged class. Yet when he meets Aline and she begins to show him that there could be another world, better one, even he starts to question everything he knows. Instead of simply ignoring her and going back to his privileged life, where he can have anything, he too decides what's right and he's not afraid to risk himself for it.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE PLOT</u>
</b><br />Breathe had an awesome and original plot. I seriously could not put this book down, because it was so intense that I constantly needed to know what was going to happen next.<br /><br />Love, lies, betrayal—oh, and death. That's another thing I loved. Sarah wasn't afraid to kill off characters, even characters who were important to our heroines and hero! And that's always a really good thing to see, if you ask me. It shows her confidence in her book and her plot.<br /><br />In a world where there's only limited air and a totalitarian government controls everything, how do you find a way to rebel? How do you leave the only home you've ever known and leave for a place where you risk running out of air? How do you stay strong when you feel like you might be dying? When those you love are dying around you? These are the kinds of difficult questions that Sarah asks, and the ones she begins to answer so beautifully.<br /><br />The plot is anything but predictable, which is great, since I've been reading way too many predictable books lately. Every twist, every turn was unexpected, and I could never tell which direction the story was going to take until it was already there. I became completely engrossed in this book, and loved everything about it.<br /><br />I loved the gorgeous world-building, too. I honestly could feel like I was actually there, and Sarah did an awesome job of making sure everything fit together and no detail was left unsaid. The world was described beautifully and there were enough visual details that you can really picture the Pod and the other places where our heroes travel to. It wasn't just a background for the plot, but played an essential role itself in the story.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE ROMANCE</u>
</b><br />Seriously, Breathe contained one of the best romances I've ever read about. When I first began, I was sure that there was going to be an irritating love triangle. I could not be happier to have been wrong! I absolutely adored the romance in this book, and the way it's a major part of the story but also doesn't monopolize the plot. It's cute and sweet and realistic. While I think it was a tad underdeveloped in the novel, I also believe that it should be given the benefit of the doubt. The underdevelopment isn't even really a major issue for me, but I did feel like I should mention it. If you read the book (which you should!) I think you'll agree with me.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE WRITING</u>
</b><br />Sarah has lovely, gorgeous, beautiful writing. I seriously love it. It's descriptive and lush without being overbearing or desperate. The voices of the individual characters really come through and their feelings are practically tangible. It's so easy to picture her world and really become Aline, Bea, and Quinn. I really don't have any complaints here—I loved it. Some of the best writing I've come across in a long time, and I could not be happier to say that.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE ENDING</u>
</b><br />Breathe ended on a cliffhanger—of course, right?—that left me desperate for more! And yet at the same time, it didn't feel like a cheap trick. Despite being desperate for the next book, I still felt entirely satisfied with this one. The ending was sweet but there were sad moments too, but overall there was the feeling of needing to move on from the past and get ready for the future, a sentiment that in a way embraces the entire ideals of these novels.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>WRAPUP</u>
</b><br />I'll definitely be reading the rest of this series, and I think i just might be a Sarah Crossan fan for life! Not only was the plot spectacular and original, but the characters were extremely likable and the writing was without a doubt incredible. I'm eagerly waiting on the next book—and trust me, after reading this, you'll be desperate to know what happens next too. Again, this is one of my all-time favorites, and I can only hope you enjoy it as much as I did! I highly recommend it.<br /><br />FINE.<br /><br />Find more of my reviews on <a href="http://sparkles-and-lightning.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Sparkles and Lightning</a>!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3337771429676142668" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer2389318462934238259">In Breathe we’re asked to imagine a world without oxygen. We don’t know why, but the world is now split into two distinct groups - the Premiums who can afford to buy the oxygen they need, and the Subs whose access is carefully rationed. People seem to be living under giant domes where everything is carefully regulated, and the truth about outside is hidden from all.<br/>We focus on three characters, from different backgrounds. Through rather tenuous links they end up together on the outside, trying t</span>
  <span id="freeText2389318462934238259" style="display:none">In Breathe we’re asked to imagine a world without oxygen. We don’t know why, but the world is now split into two distinct groups - the Premiums who can afford to buy the oxygen they need, and the Subs whose access is carefully rationed. People seem to be living under giant domes where everything is carefully regulated, and the truth about outside is hidden from all.<br />We focus on three characters, from different backgrounds. Through rather tenuous links they end up together on the outside, trying to find their way to those who want to help the world find a new way. There’s a sense of camaraderie between them, but I always got the feeling it was borne out of circumstance rather than a genuine bond.<br />This dystopian setting has all the features/elements you’d expect. It’s plotted in a way to draw you in and keep you waiting for the resolution of the main problem. For me, though, it just never quite clicked. I felt like there were a lot of characters who featured that weren’t fleshed out in a way to help me connect with them. The actual rebellion seemed to spring out of nowhere and I always got the impression people were reacting to events rather than pushing an agenda.</span>

<div id="review_379711223" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/379711223" />
    <a title="Anatea Oroz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4183325-anatea-oroz"><img alt="Anatea Oroz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545147569p2/4183325.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/379711223?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anatea Oroz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anatea Oroz" href="/user/show/4183325-anatea-oroz">Anatea Oroz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4183325-anatea-oroz?shelf=love-the-cover">love-the-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4183325-anatea-oroz?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4183325-anatea-oroz?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4183325-anatea-oroz?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer379711223" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2979975808710433988"><b>This review is also posted on my blog, <a href='http://anateasbookshelf.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Anatea's Bookshelf.</a></b><br/><br/>As soon as I saw the cover, I was in <i>love</i> with this book. The description was <i>awesome</i>, and I couldn't wait to finally read this book! It was my <b>MOST</b> anticipated fall release. And it <u>dissapointed</u> me. Yes, that's right. I didn't like it. It failed to deliver.<br/><br/>Well, I actually kinda liked the beginning. The main three characters are introduced, and we see some world building there. Oxygen has become a problem, and some citizens are moved to l</span>
  <span id="freeText2979975808710433988" style="display:none"><b>This review is also posted on my blog, <a href="http://anateasbookshelf.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Anatea's Bookshelf.</a></b><br /><br />As soon as I saw the cover, I was in <i>love</i> with this book. The description was <i>awesome</i>, and I couldn't wait to finally read this book! It was my <b>MOST</b> anticipated fall release. And it <u>dissapointed</u> me. Yes, that's right. I didn't like it. It failed to deliver.<br /><br />Well, I actually kinda liked the beginning. The main three characters are introduced, and we see some world building there. Oxygen has become a problem, and some citizens are moved to live in The Pod which is run by Breathe. Society is divided into the caste system, with Premiums who can buy oxygen and do whatever they like and Auxiliaries who have to be careful with how much oxygen they breathe in, as they have no way to pay extra oxygen. <br /><br />The more I read, the less I liked the book. The world building was unconvincing, very unconvincing! Outside the Pod, there was only 6% Oxygen in the air, but yet it was snowing, raining and whatnot. I am not an expert, but I do know that rain/snow is 1/3 Oxygen. How is that possible if there's not even enough Oxygen to breathe, if there are no plants to produce the Oxygen? There are so many questions, and yet, almost none of them were answered. Some of them will probably be answered in the next book, but I really think they were necessary in this one. <br /><br />The story is narrated in first person by Alina, Quinn, and Bea. I did not like it at all. I had to, more than just a few times, check on who's POV it was again. They all sounded the same, even though Quinn is a guy and you'd expect to recognize his POV, but sometimes I just couldn't. <br /><br />The romance in this book, oh dear God, even now I have a headache if I just think about it. Let me just explain it to you and see for yourselves. We have Bea who's Quinns best friend and is madly in love with him, but of course, he doesn't notice it because he is in love with Alina. I don't have to mention that he doesn't know her at all, but he follows her around like a love-sick puppy. Everything would be okay if Alina returned the feelings, but no, she was grieving the boy who got killed because of her. Already rolling your eyes? This isn't even half of it, but I won't reveal more as it includes some spoilers.<br /><br />Now about the characters. <br /><u>Alina.</u> The only thing I like about this girl is her name, it's really pretty. And that's where my affection towards this girl ends. She was rude most of the time, she is cold and she cares only about herself. Alina is part of The Resistance, group of people who stood up to Breathe. While her intentions are sometimes right, her actions are not.<br /><u>Quinn.</u> He is a Premium and he doesn't know how hard life can get. Most of the time he's clueless about everything and the only thing he cares about are girls. Everything came easy to him because he was a Premium, but when he found out about certain things, he took control, and I like him just a little bit better because of it. <br /><u>Bea.</u> I liked her the best even though she was whiny and sometimes even irritating. She didn't want any of it to happen, she just wanted to enjoy her time with Quinn, but Alina ruined it all and Bea was stuck somewhere where she didn't want to be. <br /><br />Overall, I didn't like this book, I won't be reading a sequel and I wouldn't recommend this book to anyone, but the fact that I didn't like the book doesn't necessary means you won't either.<br /><br /><b><a href="http://anateasbookshelf.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/anateaoroz" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/AnateasAdventures" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://instagram.com/anateaoroz/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/anateaoroz/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="2979975808710433988" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_288265968" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/288265968" />
    <a title="Emilija" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4460175-emilija"><img alt="Emilija" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476126551p2/4460175.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/288265968?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emilija" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emilija" href="/user/show/4460175-emilija">Emilija</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781408827192" href="/book/show/13541378-breathe">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4460175-emilija?shelf=2013-reads">2013-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4460175-emilija?shelf=read-first-book-in-series">read-first-book-in-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4460175-emilija?shelf=series-i-abandoned">series-i-abandoned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer288265968" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4952700604428852995">Breathe conjured up a lot of unexpected emotions, a lot of realizations and a fuck load of thought provoking questions.<br/><br/>The reason why Breathe made me emotional at times is definitely not because of the characters - I'll get to that later - but of the world that the book was set in. The author had a look at the world today, saw that global warming is a huge problem that isn't really being solved, took the idea and ran with it.<br/><br/>Books like this - especially this one - make me irrationally paranoid a</span>
  <span id="freeText4952700604428852995" style="display:none">Breathe conjured up a lot of unexpected emotions, a lot of realizations and a fuck load of thought provoking questions.<br /><br />The reason why Breathe made me emotional at times is definitely not because of the characters - I'll get to that later - but of the world that the book was set in. The author had a look at the world today, saw that global warming is a huge problem that isn't really being solved, took the idea and ran with it.<br /><br />Books like this - especially this one - make me irrationally paranoid at 3 am whilst tumblin' because my brain suddenly starts to think that a future like this has the potential to come true in the very very very far future, because carbon emission levels are getting higher, deforestation is happening faster and governments are becoming more corrupt by the second, taking advantage of their countries and abusing their power. We see this everywhere, in our world and in all of the other worlds that exists within book pages.<br /><br />After reading this book I realized one very big thing, and I knew this pretty much from the beginning of time but I've never given the thought my time to actually think about it as much as I have now and that is: there are no good guys. Ever. Let me elaborate. There are good, nice people and they might do something for a good cause, but that does not mean that they are the 'good' guys because everyone in their mind is 'good' and 'right'. The saying 'there are two sides to every story' has much more meaning to me now. There are no good guys in Breathe. The resistance people aren't the good guys. You'll see what I mean when you read the book yourself.<br /><br />I understand that this is a series but a lot of things weren't discussed and further explored in this book and that really, really bothered me. First of all, the Pod Minister was a very huge character in the book and to just completely not talk about how he died was just disrespectful to the readers. I personally was pissed off at the fact that we weren't shown how he died, all we got was 'He's dead'. That's it. The author also touched on this water issue and it's all so hazy and cryptic and I was just like "WTF" but I'm pretty sure that's her hook for the second book in the series.<br /><br />You don't have to expect much from this book. If you're looking for a fresh breath of air - more specifically in the dystopian genre - look somewhere else. We've all seen this plot before; a corrupt government, a resistance group, a battle between the two. Been there, read that.<br /><br />Now for the characters. Quinn is a stupid fuck that was a waste of their precious air. God fucking damn, he was so whinny and just a plain pain in the ass. Same with Bree, why the hell was she even there? The story could have been exactly the same without her, she contributed nothing - again, she was a waste of their precious air. Alina. At the beginning I liked her a lot. I liked that she was a heartless bitch, I really <i>really</i> did. But as the story progressed she kept disappointing me more and more and now there's nothing left for me to like here anymore.<br /><br />I. JUST. RHYMED.<br /><br />I AM SO FUCKING DONE WITH THIS.<br /><br />OH AND ALSO, NOTICE HOW THE SYNOPSIS SAYS "WHO ARE THEY PROTECTING THEM FROM?" IN RELATION TO THE TREES? WELL FUCKING GEE I REALLY DO WONDER WHO THE RESISTANCE IS HIDING THE TREES FROM. FUCKING DAMN SHIT GOT ME HEATED. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4952700604428852995" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/364711740" />
    <a title="Jen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5616772-jen"><img alt="Jen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1391659353p2/5616772.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/364711740?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen" href="/user/show/5616772-jen">Jen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5616772-jen?shelf=arc-s">arc-s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5616772-jen?shelf=alt-pov">alt-pov</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer364711740" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7969225682709842061">2.75 stars<br/><br/>A BIG "Thanks" to Jenn from the YA Sisterhood for loaning me her copy, she ROCKS!<br/><br/>OK, so, this is one of those books that I was really, really excited to read but ended up struggling to finish. The concept is interesting, the story well written, and the characters; while engaging, were also annoying a lot of the time. <br/><br/>Bea and Quinn have been BFF's forever and of course, she's in love with him and he's as clueless as ever. (silly book boy) Air is the hot commodity that is controlled by t</span>
  <span id="freeText7969225682709842061" style="display:none">2.75 stars<br /><br />A BIG "Thanks" to Jenn from the YA Sisterhood for loaning me her copy, she ROCKS!<br /><br />OK, so, this is one of those books that I was really, really excited to read but ended up struggling to finish. The concept is interesting, the story well written, and the characters; while engaging, were also annoying a lot of the time. <br /><br />Bea and Quinn have been BFF's forever and of course, she's in love with him and he's as clueless as ever. (silly book boy) Air is the hot commodity that is controlled by the government and they decide who gets more and who doesn't If you're a Premium (like Quinn) your life is generally better and longer than say, Bea's who comes from the wrong side of the tram stop. While she may dream of a life with Quinn, it's really just that, a dream because Auxiliaries and Premiums don't belong together. <br /><br />Quinn is your stereotypical rich boy whose oblivious to all he's privileged to and Alina, the beautiful girl Quinn falls for, is a rebel looking for change. If they were political parties, Alina would be the far left, Quinn the far right and Bea, the moderate that balances them out and helps them see reason. I found Quinn to be a bit of a whiner and it doesn't matter how hot a guy (or girl) is, whining is a downer. Alina may be pretty but her selfishness overpowers her beauty and I just didn't care for her. I liked Bea most because she's smart, compassionate, selfless and focused on the bigger picture, whereas the other two are too caught up in themselves to notice much else. (Potential spoiler - Quinn and Bea have known each other for YEARS and he doesn't know what color her eyes are. WHAT?!) <br /><br />Alina is pining away for someone she believes is dead as a result of her choices and Quinn is caught up in playing Alina's knight in shining armour because he's convinced she's his dream girl. He eventually learns that what he's really looking for and what he needs has been in front of him all along but at what cost?<br /><br />For as frustrating as this book was for me, all of the characters have opportunities to make changes for the better not only for themselves, but for the world around them too. This is part of a trilogy so it will be interesting to see how it all pans outs and who will survive. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7969225682709842061" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_10535458'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10535458-glitch"><img alt="Glitch (Glitch, #1)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1326131169l/10535458._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xeL9cVQknmX9axgIN7l5u09AmjMuPifWFuNQEukqNgTjaL7mLl4gVIspglIn2DARsThxlztkXbWKqzvzFVY/6A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('J3/yH8IzvE4R2DXzNhNMulNitOfJn1sX8lawgBhoij8B9bGIuEkCf2ear6kmcgUQrRpfQ9zFIXRuHtth5BSD0w==')})
  }

When her one chance at happiness is ripped away with breathtaking cruelty, emotions she\'s always had but never understood are unleashed. As rage, terror, and desire threaten to overwhelm her, Elysia must find the will to survive. <span id="freeTextContainer5856376858605454175">Sarah Crossan is Irish. She graduated with a degree in Philosophy and Literature before training as an English and Drama teacher at Cambridge University and worked to promote creative writing in schools before leaving teaching to write full time. <br/><br/>She completed her Masters in Creative Writing at the University of Warwick in 2003 and in 2010 received an Edward Albee Fellowship for writing.<br/><br/>She curren</span>
  <span id="freeText5856376858605454175" style="display:none">Sarah Crossan is Irish. She graduated with a degree in Philosophy and Literature before training as an English and Drama teacher at Cambridge University and worked to promote creative writing in schools before leaving teaching to write full time. <br /><br />She completed her Masters in Creative Writing at the University of Warwick in 2003 and in 2010 received an Edward Albee Fellowship for writing.<br /><br />She currently lives in NYC. <br /></span>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/16484181-breathe">Quotes from Breathe</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;I allow myself to be right here, in the moment, savouring the peace. All the millions and millions of stars remind me, too, how small and fragile I am.
